text:
So far this produced the thinnest crust pizza, which is what we were looking for. I used this recipe and made two pizzas with it. With the first pizza I prebaked the crust for 10 minutes on the middle rack (on a pizza stone) then added the toppings. It was thin but the middle of the pizza could have been crispier. With the second pizza, I prebaked it for ten minutes on the lowest rack in the oven, added the toppings and returned it to the lowest rack to finish. This made a BIG difference. This was incredibly easy to make. *****Update*****I've made this several times now and have gotten my technique down on how to get it nice and thin and CRISPY! :) I divide the dough in half and use one half per pizza. After spreading it on my stone, I bake it for 10 minutes on the lowest rack at 500 degrees. Then I lower the temp to 450, add the toppings and bake til the cheese is bubbly. When you bite into the crust you can actually hear it crunch! SO so so happy I tried this recipe :)

text:
I have tried many of the pizza dough recipes on this site to get the "perfect pizza parlor" crust.  there have been several that were not too good and some that were great.  But in the end This pizza recipe by far is the best.  I made no changes to the actual ingredients.  I only added a tsp per cup of flour of King Arthur Pizza seasoning that a friend recommended to me.  But the crust was great with or without the seasoning.  (fabulous with the seasoning and I highly recommend it!).  I played around with the cooking temps and time and found 500 degrees bottome shelf for 5 minutes for pre cook and 450 for about 15-20 on the next shelf up with toppings. I am a happy girl...now I move onto toppings.  thanks to all of your responses.  This site helped me in my quest for a great homemade crust.

text:
This was my first attempt at a homemade pizza crust and it turned out great!  I threw in about 1/4 cup of wheat bran to kick up the health factor a bit and also used a pizza stone to bake the crust on.  Before spreading the dough on the pizza stone, I spread a bit of corn meal on the stone, which baked into the dough and gave the crust an extra crunch.  I also baked the pizza for a full 20 minutes and the crust came out a beautiful golden brown color, but I think next time I'll bake for an additional 5 minutes or so, as I prefer an extra crispy crust.  All in all, this was a great recipe, and I'll definitely use it again!

text:
An Absolutely wonderful crust! I finally bought a couple of pizza stones. (No need to prebake for 5 mins)I just sprinkle a little course cornmeal on the preheated stone and make the pizza.  (Original review: Before I had the pizza stones.)  Okay! I have a family of eight. This pizza dough was QUICK, EASY, and DELICIOUS. I followed the recipe exactly, anything I added to it was after I made the dough. (Next time I will add some spice to it when mixing and I'm pretty sure it will turn out great.) This dough takes on any flavor/spice well. I did a cheese stuffed crust pizza, two regular pizzas and a garlic crust pizza. Yummy! I did place my crust in a heated oven for 5 mins. I did the same thing with the stuffed crust also. I then finished making up the pizza and baked it for 15 mins. Everbody loves this pizza crust. (The dough will seem sticky after you mix it together. DO NOT add more flour. Just let it stand for 10 mins. Then just put a little olive oil on your fingers and work the dough into place on you pan.) This one is a keeper.

text:
This is an excellent crust.  I've made it three times in two days.  I mixed it in a mixing bowl with my Kitchen Aid and the flat beater.  I dumped it on a large pizza pan and pressed it as thin as possible.  I drizzled with olive oil, topped with cheese and then pepperoni and jalapenos.  I baked at 450 degrees until browned and it was really good.  The second one was pretty much the same.  For the third one, I mixed it up in the Kitchen Aid but let it rise for two hours.  I pressed it onto the large pizza pan as thin as possible making a really nice thick edge.  I drizzled with olive oil and added chesse and then pepperoni and italian seasoning.  I baked at 450 also and it was really, really good.  This crust is so easy - keep working with it until you can make it the way you like it.  It was extremely easy!  Have fun!

text:
I have made this crust many times, but I always add 1/4 tsp. of garlic powder, 1/4 tsp. of onion powder, and 1/4 tsp. of pizza seasoning to my flour, so I don't know how it is without them, but I do know that every time I have made this crust, everyone has loved it. I have used all purpose flour, bread flour, and also whole wheat flour...all winners. I have made this crust also as deep dish pizza, and also makes a nice thin crust, in other words...very versatile. If this crust didn't turn out right, I'm sure you made a slight mistake, and that happens sometime, but try it again...carefully. Thanks Valentino for such lovely and quick crust. Oh yeah, I forgot...I have also used honey in place of the sugar when I used the whole wheat flour.

text:
Outstanding recipe.  For future cooks, read this: Let the dough rise for 30 minutes, covered with a towel, rather than letting it rest for just 10 minutes.  Then sprinkle 1/4 cup of extra flour on a surface and knead the dough for 5-7 minutes, or until dough has absorbed the flour.  This will help you roll it out better and it will rise beautifully in the oven.

text:
Really good pizza crust. I followed recipe exactly and didn't feel the dough was too sticky to handle at all. I added garlic powder to the crust and divided the crust to make two thin crust pizzas. I don't have a pizza stone so I just used a regular cookie sheet, greased just a little with some shortening. I topped with canned pizza sauce, mozz and chedder cheese and some dried basil. The kids loved it and so did I. A nice quick meal and something you can do a lot with. On the second pizza, after I took it out of the oven, I took it off the cookie sheet and put it back in the oven for a few minutes to really crisp up the crust. Will definitely make again! Thanks!

text:
This crust is great, but I have to add just a few caveats:

1) I had to let the dough sit in a warm place for more like 30-45 minutes in order for it to rise.
2) I needed to bake the pizza for a bit longer than required in order for the crust to cook through completely.
3) It made enough for two pizza stone's worth of pizza.  However, I had vastly different results for each stone.  On my older pizza stone, which has been used for years, the crust did not stick at all.  However, on my much newer pizza stone, the crust stuck to the bottom and is impossible to get off, which kind of ruins the pizza.  I would definitely suggest dusting the pizza stones with flour or cooking spray before putting the dough on.  I'm wondering if the reason the crust didn't stick to the old one is because it has years of build-up (maybe similar to a much-used cast iron skillet?).  But who knows. 

Flavor is great, texture is great, and home-made crust is so much better than store-bought.

text:
AWESOME recipe! here's a couple additonal tricks & tips (my boyfriend used to work at Godfather's pizza and helped me make it!) : 1.) After spreading the dough on the baking pan into your desired shape/size, place the dough in your preheated oven for about 3-5 minutes. This will help the dough rise without actually cooking it (common trick of baking loaves of bread). Then take the dough out and you press it with your hands to make it larger/flatter/whatever you want. This is also a good time to shape the crust of the pizza because the forms you make will stay unlike when the dough is completely new on the pan. We added a lot of parmesan, garlic powder, and oregano to the dough. It was VERY good. The cheese makes the dough stickier when kneading it, you can put a little olive oil or butter (will make the crust nice and light brown) to help stop the stick. I will ALWAYS use this nice, EASY, delicious recipe. :] Thanks so much!

text:
I tried a few variations of different pizza dough, and this is by far the easiest to work with for me.  I started making homemade pizza so that I can shape the pizza to bake in my toaster oven.  My husband and I both love thin crust, and this recipe can make 3 portion of 10 inch by 10 inch thin crust pizza  (I have stretch it to make 4 portion of super thin crust).  I just put all the ingredients in my bread machine to let it knead for 10 minutes.  I don't own a pizza stone yet, but I find that pre-baking the crust first to a light golden brown at your highest temperature setting before adding your toppings really makes a difference.  I also let it rise in the fridge at least overnight.  It's not necessary, but I always have a hard time rolling out pizza dough.  If I let it sit for at least a day or two in the fridge (after I portion out the dough), I can just press the dough into whatever shape and it doesn't bounce back.  Excellent recipe!

I love this pizza dough!!! I use it at least twice a week because I have a house full of boys that love pizza. This is easy to make and i also rub the crust with olive oil before baking. I bake the crust 5 minutes by itself and then take it out of the oven, add the toppings, and bake for 10 more minutes. I find that the crust is way crispier when I do it that way...Then when I get it out of the oven fully done, I make garlic butter and brush it on the outside crust and let it set for a minute or two....AMAZING!!!

text:
I have never reviewed a recipe online, and I've found some incredible ones.  That should give you an idea of just how delicious this pizza dough is!!!  The only change I made was to add basil, oregano, and thyme to the dough.  Keep in mind that the dough will be very sticky after it's mixed, but it will be much easier to work with after it's risen.  Be patient, and DO NOT add more flour!!!  Also, the direction don't say this, but it's important... be sure to spray the pan with non-stick cooking spray before putting the pizza dough on it!

text:
I previously rated this with only 4 stars because the first time I made it into only one pizza, and it was way too thick, but this has become a recipe I use several times a week and love! It makes two, not overly thin, thin-crust pizzas. It's easy, fast, and delicious. The trick is that you just have to really work it down to a thin crust, just like the way those pizza dough packets work. Do this by patting it with fingers, spinning it in the air, or rolling it with a rolling pin.

text:
My favourite, easy, quick, basic pizza dough. I have  used this recipe for years now. I usually make it as written, but sometimes I have fun with the recipe. Some of the ingredients I've mixed into the dough include (in various combos): garlic powder, Italian seasoning, thyme, basil, grated or chunks of cheddar cheese, grated Parmesan cheese, bacon, etc. I've successfully used the dough to make mini deep-fried pizza pockets, pizza rolls, calzones, pizza bread, frozen mini pizzas. I've also baked it in the toaster oven, on the bbq on a pizza stone and as mentioned, deep-fried. It's always comes out perfectly awesome. And it can be ready in 30 minutes. That's faster than driving to the store for a frozen pizza!

This crust was perfect for our 'Reuben Pizza' from AR.  I did have to add quite a bit more flour as our humidity level was at 92% today.  I threw the ingredients in my Kitchen Aid and let it do the work.  Once the dough was made, I left for yoga class and when I got home, it had risen, a lot. Since I was making a Reuben pizza, I added caraway seeds to the crust and that added great flavor.  Yes, I would use this crust again.

text:
This recipe is amazing, I looked at a lot of other crust recipes, when I started wanting to make my own pizza dough & I'm glad I went with this 1! Have made it so many times I've memorized the recipe! This recipe makes plenty of crust, for cheap... I made 3 of these crusts for my family & it fed 10-12 of us! I usually just half the amount of dough I make (if there's some you don't use roll it out & put in the freezer), put it on a cookie sheet & it's good to go! 
**THE MOST IMPORTANT THING TO REMEMBER ABOUT THIS RECIPE IS TO PUT IT IN THE OVEN... THEN AFTER ABOUT 7-8 MINUTES TAKE IT OUT & ADD YOUR SAUCE & TOPPINGS! This is THE BEST WAY TO KEEP THE CRUST CRISPY!
One day I let the crust rise for extra time & didn't notice a difference at all in the taste of the pizza or the consistency of my dough. Hope this helps!

text:
As a qualifier, please note that I'm yeast recipe challenged - I simply cannot get dough recipes to turn out right no matter what I try. This recipe was so easy that even I made an unbelievably tasty, flaky pizza from scratch in under one hour. I followed all the steps exactly and used a Kitchenaid mixer dough attachment just until the dough was blended (not to over mix). I then spread this perfect amount of dough for 1 two person pizza onto a pizza pan (holes on bottom) and brushed it with olive oil seasoned with all sorts of Italian herbs and roasted garlic, etc. before adding toppings. Baked for 15 mins at 400 and it was phenomenal texture, taste and thickness (imagine medium thick with an end piece no one wants to waste). My picky husband loved it too. It could not have been more straightforward or tastier. Please try it!

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
I love this pizza crust! Although, and this could be considered a con - it is so easy to put together I probably have it too often, now!

I don't have a pizza stone, so I split the dough in two and use a half-sheet baking sheet for one of them, which is perfectly sized. I usually make it just for me, and put half in a covered bowl in the fridge, where it keeps fine for a couple of days.

I recommend adding some oregano, basil, and/or thyme to the dough itself, rather than sprinkling on top. I haven't tried a dessert variation yet, but it's been good with every savory topping I've tried so far. Highly recommended.

Bit of advice, though - don't make it too thick. I like 'deep dish' crusts, but this can be a bit too dense and chewy even for me if I don't shape it thinly. Trust me, even rolled thin, it is very good, and quite sturdy.

Good pizza dough. I like mine a little thinner so I used bread flour and kneaded it for about ten minutes then let it rest in refrigerator for 20 to 30 min. This seems to help make it more thin and crispy. Don't forget to proof before adding sauce and toppings. I also added a bit more salt, Italian seasoning and granulated garlic. It also helps to butter the outside crust ring before putting it into the oven. Hope you enjoy!!

This crust is delicious and so easy. I usually use my mixer with a dough hook, but just mix it enough to combine everything. Over mixing creates a tougher crust. I also add in a tablespoon (or more!) of Italian Seasoning to add some flavor to the crust. And then before pre-baking the crust, I spread on a lightly cooked butter/garlic mixture. Good stuff.  I made this as directed, leaving the dough still a bit wet and pressing it into a baking pan.  I thought I'd be clever by laying it out real thin since I don't tend to prefer thick, chewy pizza dough (I'm more into thin and crispy).  Even so, it rose quite a bit.  This ended up okay since my family ended up eating it all and they love thick crust pizza.

My uncle, who doesn't really believe in compliments, said it was some of the best pizza he'd ever had.

The only change I made, one which I thought worked out really well, was to sprinkle herb de provence over the crust after I put it in the baking sheet.  The crust itself is mild in flavor and the rosemary, thyme, basil, etc. complimented it nicely.

text:
For a pizza crust that didn't require rising, it was very good.   It was fairly quick and very easy.  I used bread flour instead of regular flour and I added about 1/2 more flour than called for; without the extra flour it seemed too gooey.  That may not happen if you use regular flour, which I didn't have on hand at the time.   I also used a pizza stone instead of a pan; just sprinkled from cornmeal first so it didn't stick.  I then put the sauce on it and baked it for about ten minutes and THEN put the toppings and cheese on it and cooked about another 15 minutes.  I will definitely make this again, especially when short on time and craving pizza!

text:
Ive been using this recipe for three years and my family still loves it.  It works great for your general pizza toppings as well as for breakfast pizzas. Tips: cover your dough bowl with a thin cloth while its at rest  to help maintain temp for your yeast. Work the dough so its smooth and shape on parchment paper. Dont forget to poke some small holes in the bottom to keep the crust from getting air bubbles. Try sprinkling flour on your pizza pan lightly after oiling to get the crust to slide off easily. Brush crust edges with olive oil and a touch of garlic salt.

text:
I really liked this crust! I followed the recipe, and made 1 large 14" pizza crust. I preheated the oven to 450 degrees with my pizza stone in the oven on the lowest rack. I formed the dough on a piece of parchment paper, the same size as my stone, and slid it onto the stone with my pizza peel. I pre-baked my crust for 10 minutes, lowering the temp to 425 after putting the crust on the stone. I removed the crust from the oven, slipping the pizza peel between the crust and the parchment, and then left it cool on top of the pizza peel on the kitchen counter.  When it was time to bake, I preheated the oven to 425 with the stone on the middle rack this time. I added the toppings and slid the pizza directly on the stone and baked for another 6 minutes, then switching the oven to broil for about another 4 minutes until the fresh mozzarella on top starting to bubble and brown. The crust was about 1/4" thick, and nicely brown on the bottom and edges, with a slight crunch to it. Would use this recipe and method again! Thanks!

text:
Excellent  pizza crust.  I made the dough in my mixer using a dough hook. I used a pizza pan with lots of holes in the bottom of the pan.  The crust baked just fine.  I also did as another reviewer suggested: place the dough  in the pan on the lowest rack and bake in preheated oven at 500* for 10 mins.  Then remove the crust and top it with sauce, cheese and toppings. Return the pan to using the middle rack and bake at 450* for an additional 15 mins. My family gave it rave reviews. The crust was nice and crispy as we like it.
Thank you goes to both the author for a great recipe and to the  reviewer with a great baking suggestion!!

text:
I made this crust tonight and wow it is so easy to make. I love the simple ingredients and prep to cook time. The only change I made was using bread flour instead of AP flour. I really never buy any flour besides AP but I thought I'd try it and I'm glad I did. The bread flour really helped to crisp up the crust. I spread the crust onto a baking sheet and baked it at 500 for 5-10 minutes (I forgot the exact time but somewhere between these, just keep an eye on it). I took it out, spread pizza sauce, cheese, and toppings on top and baked it at 450 for 15-20 minutes. The crust was good but next time I think I will make 2 pizzas so I get really super thin crusts which are my favorite. Overall, a tasty and easy crust recipe and I will use again.

text:
This was a really good crust that baked very well. I will definitely use it again.  I made it according to the recipe and cooked it on a baking stone.  I brushed the edges of the crust with olive oil after it was dressed.  I added a sprinkle of cornmeal onto the preheated baking stone and it did not stick at all - it slid off onto the peel with ease!  When the pizza was sliced, you could pick it up and the pizza did not droop at all as the crust was perfectly crispy with a nice golden color.  The only part about it was that it didn't have a lot of flavor which could be easily fixed by taking the advise on the recipe and using seasonings on the crust or even in the dough.  I only used seasonings atop the cheese so will use seasoning in the crust next time.

text:
I followed the recipe ingredients exactly, but let it rest for closer to 20-25 minutes.  I spread the dough out onto a lightly oiled pan sprinkled with corn meal.  Then I sprinkled the top of the dough with oregano, basil, and a little garlic powder.  Baked on the lower rack of the oven for 5 minutes, then took out and added sauce, minced garlic, and mozzarella & provolone cheeses, and brushed the crust edges with a little olive oil.  Baked for approx 14 more minutes on the middle rack.  Pizza was very good, and the crust was very thick, which I like.  So if you like thin crusts, you'll want to use a very large pan or make two pizzas with this recipe.  I will definitely make this again!

text:
I have tried a lot of different recipes for pizza crust before and this one is tops.  I will say before I start that the first time I made this recipe I followed the directions as written except I got busy during the 10 min rise time and it ended up being more like 30 or 40 min.  It turned out so good that I decided to just stick with the extra rise time, each time I've made it.  This makes a lot of dough.  I usually double the batch and freeze half of it.  Mine has always come out thick like a deep dish pizza, however, it's not to dense.  My husband raves about how good the pizza is every time I make it.  Says it's better than any where we could order in or get take out from.  My most recent experiment with this recipe was to try and make it a little more healthy.  So I used one cup of whole wheat flour and a cup and a half of spelt flour, I double the batch so the other 2.5 cups were A.P. flour.  It really worked well and I think next time I'll just do away with the A.P. flour all together.  Additionally on my last experiment with this recipe I also substituted the sugar for honey.  It worked out quite nicely.  If you don't want a thick crust then you can just cut the rise time or let it rise and then just spread the dough out real thin.  If you want it thin you can probably get almost 2 pizza out of the recipe as listed.  
Thank you Jody for sharing this very tasty recipe.

I will definitely be using the recipe again! I was so surprised how good it turned out. I did not think it would with how easy the directions were! It was pretty sticky, therefore it was too hard to get onto the stone that was already in the oven preheating. With my first pizza I slipped it onto the stone once the crust crisped up and cooked it the rest of the way on the stone. One of the best pizza crust recipes I have found so far.  I substitute a tsp of garlic salt for the salt and then add 1/2 tsp of salt.  I also add 1 tsp of basil, and 1 tsp of oregano to the mixture before adding the flour.  I use a 9x13 glass pan greased with olive oil.  The crust turns out with just enough crunch and tastes great.  I love it with a white sauce... (butter, garlic, olive oil, oregano and basil) and top it with tomato slices and nicely seasoned boneless skinless chicken tenderloins... Great!!

I know, I know, I shouldn't rate a recipe that I make a ton of changes on but I thought it might help others.  This was great! I used kosher salt instead of regular, added a couple of shakes of garlic powder and a hefty pinch of Italian seasoning to the liquid portion before mixing in the flour.  I used it for calzones instead of pizza and as I don't have a baking stone I preheated my cast iron skillet and baked on it on a piece of parchment paper.  Will definately make again!  Very flavorful and the texture was nice and fluffy.

text:
I have been making homemade pizza for my family for several years.  We recently moved and I misplaced my basic dough recipe, so I searched on the site and picked this dough to make.  My family LOVED it!  They told me I didn't have to keep looking for the old recipe! :0)

I did add a bit more sugar.  And note, the dough is pretty sticky so you'll be tempted to add more flour but don't!  I'm convinced that's why it bakes up so nicely!  Also, I prebaked my dough in the pizza pan for about 15 minutes to make sure it would cook all the way through, then added toppings & cheese and baked for another 15 minutes.  I topped it off with about a minute and a half under the broiler.  

All the way around, this pizza crust was great!  It reminded my husband and I of Uno's Restaurant in Chicago.  5 stars for sure!

text:
I am foremost rating this on ease.  I could think of many scenarios when this recipe would be at one's fingertips. (unexpected company, sudden craving)  I didn't change anything.  I spread this out onto a cookie sheet and baked for 17 minutes (thinner crust) **I sprayed my fingertips with cooking spray and that worked like a charm!** There was no doughiness at all in the middle(and I used fresh sliced tomatoes)  I used this on a chicken garlic pizza so the crust was brushed w/alot of garlic and herbs so honestly, couldn't tell if the crust was bland.  I don't care for a thinner crust but this is great in a pinch.
